Question: Mr.Sam takes 17 hours to go by train to a certain city and return by car. He loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train. How long would he have taken if he had traveled by car in both ways?
Choices:
  A: 22 hrs
  B: 18 hrs
  C: 16 hrs
  D: 20 hrs
  E: 13 hrs
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the time it takes Mr. Sam to travel to the city by train is "x" hours.
  Then, the time it takes him to return by car would also be "x" hours.
  According to the problem, he takes 17 hours to go by train to the city and return by car.
  Therefore, the total time taken by Mr. Sam = x + x + 17 = 2x + 17.
  The problem also states that he loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train.
  This means that the time it takes him to travel both ways by train = 2x + 4.
  We can now set up an equation: 2x + 4 + 17 = 2x + 2x.
  Solving for x, we get x = 7.
  Therefore, the time it takes Mr. Sam to travel by car in both ways = 2x = 14 hours.
  The answer is D: 20 hrs.
Action: Answer("D")

  We need to find the minimum number of copper coins that the diver brought, which is represented by x.

  20(2) + 25y = 340
  40 + 25y = 340
  25y = 300
  y = 12
  This means that the diver brought 2 copper coins and 12 brass coins.

  A: 368
  B: 377
  C: 288
  D: 997
  E: 112

  From the problem, we know that a+b+c=17 and a^2+b^2+c^2=109.
  We also know that 100a+10b+c-495=100c+10b+a.
  Simplifying the equation above, we get 99a-99c=594 or a-c=6.
  We can use the equation a-c=6 to solve for a and c in terms of b.
  We know that a+b+c=17, so a+c=17-b.

  Since a, b, and c are digits, they must be integers.

Response 1:
Thought:
  Let the three-digit number be represented by ABC, where A, B, and C are digits.
  We know that A + B + C = 17 and A^2 + B^2 + C^2 = 109.
  We also know that 100A + 10B + C - 495 = 100C + 10B + A.
  Simplifying the equation above, we get 99A - 99C = 495, which gives A - C = 5.
  We can use the first two equations to solve for B and C in terms of A.
  From A + B + C = 17, we get B = 17 - A - C.
  From A^2 + B^2 + C^2 = 109, we get B^2 = 109 - A^2 - C^2.
  Substituting B = 17 - A - C into the second equation above, we get (17 - A - C)^2 = 109 - A^2 - C^2.
  Expanding both sides and simplifying, we get 2AC + 2A - 2C = 36.
  Factoring out 2, we get 2(A - 1)(C + 1) = 36.
  Since A and C are digits, we know that A - 1 and C + 1 are factors of 18.
  The possible pairs of (A - 1, C + 1) are (1, 18), (2, 9), (3, 6), and (6, 3).
  We can check each pair to see if it satisfies the equations we have.
  The only pair that works is (6, 3), which gives A = 7, B = 3, and C = 4.
  Therefore, the three-digit number is 734, and the answer is A: 368.

Question: The ratio of the volumes of a cube to that of the sphere which will fit inside the cube is?
Choices:
  A: 2: π
  B: 7:2
  C: 8:2
  D: 6: π
  E: 8:3

  The volume of the cube is a^3. 
  The volume of the sphere is (4/3)πr^3 = (4/3)π(a/2)^3 = (1/6)πa^3. 
  The ratio of the volumes of the cube to the sphere is a^3 : (1/6)πa^3 = 6:π.
  Therefore, the answer is D: 6:π.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 76 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: All 250 files on Sam's hard drive are infected by either a virus or a worm or both. The number of files that are infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm. If 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, how many of Sam's files were NOT infected by a worm?
Choices:
  A: 50
  B: 70
  C: 75
  D: 100
  E: 125
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Let's use a Venn diagram to represent the information given in the problem.
  Let x be the number of files infected only by a virus.
  Let y be the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm.
  Let z be the number of files infected only by a worm.
  We know that x + y + z = 250.
  We also know that z = 2.5y.
  We know that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, so x + y = 125.
  We can substitute z = 2.5y into the first equation to get x + y + 2.5y = 250.
  Simplifying this equation, we get x + 3.5y = 250.
  We can substitute x + y = 125 into this equation to get y = 50.
  Therefore, z = 2.5y = 125.
  The number of files that were not infected by a worm is x, which is the number of files infected only by a virus.
  We know that x + y = 125, so x = 125 - y = 75.
  Therefore, the answer is C: 75.

  The answer is 0.

Response 3:
Thought:
  Let's use a Venn diagram to represent the information given in the question.
  We know that the total number of files is 250.
  Let's use "V" to represent the set of files infected by a virus, and "W" to represent the set of files infected by a worm.
  We know that the number of files infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm.
  Let's use "x" to represent the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm.
  Then the number of files infected only by a worm is 2.5x.
  We can fill in the Venn diagram as follows:
  - The number of files infected by a virus only is V - x.
  - The number of files infected by a worm only is W - 2.5x.
  - The number of files infected by both a virus and a worm is x.
  We also know that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus.
  This means that the number of files not infected by a virus is 0.5 * 250 = 125.
  We want to find the number of files that were not infected by a worm.
  Let's use "y" to represent this number.
  Then we can set up the following equation:
  y = 125 - V + x
  We can solve for V by using the fact that the number of files infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm:
  W - 2.5x = 2.5x
  W = 5x
  V = 125 - W - x
  V = 125 - 5x - x
  V = 125 - 6x
  Now we can substitute this expression for V into the equation we set up earlier:
  y = 125 - (125 - 6x) + x
  y = 6x
  We know that x + 2.5x + (125 - 6x) + y = 250 (the total number of files), so:
  3.5x + y = 125
  We can solve these two equations simultaneously to get:
  x = 20
  y = 70
  Therefore, the answer is B: 70.

  n(U) = 250 (total number of files)
  n(A) = 125 (50% of the files were not infected by a virus)
  n(A ∪ B) = n(A) + n(B) - n(A ∩ B)
  n(B) = 250 - n(A' ∩ B') = 250 - (n(U) - n(A) - n(B) + n(A ∩ B))
  Simplifying the equation above, we get:
  n(B) = n(A) + n(A ∩ B) - n(A' ∩ B') - 250
  Substituting the values we know, we get:
  n(B) = 125 + x - 2.5x - 250
  n(B) = -1.5x - 125

  0 ≤ -1.5x - 125

  This is possible, so we have found the correct values of x and y.
  We want to find the number of files that are not infected by a worm.
  n(B') = n(U) - n(B)

  n(B) = 35 + (125 - y) + 0
  n(B) = 160 - y
  n(B') = 250 - (160 - y) = 90 + y
  n(B') = 90 + 35 = 125
  Therefore, the number of files that are NOT infected by a worm is 125.

Question: A trader sold an article at a profit of 20% for Rs.360. What is the cost price of the article?
Choices:
  A: 270
  B: 300
  C: 280
  D: 320
  E: 315
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let the cost price of the article be x.
  Profit percentage = 20%
  Selling price = Cost price + Profit
  Selling price = x + 0.2x = 1.2x
  Given, Selling price = Rs.360
  1.2x = 360
  x = 360/1.2
  x = 300
  Therefore, the cost price of the article is Rs.300.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let CP be the cost price of the article.
  Profit% = 20%
  Selling price = Rs.360
  We know that Selling price = Cost price + Profit
  So, 360 = CP + 20% of CP
  360 = CP + 0.2CP
  360 = 1.2CP
  CP = 360/1.2
  CP = 300
  Therefore, the cost price of the article is Rs.300.

Question: A newspaper costs $4 on Sunday and $1 the rest of the days of the week. If a hotel orders twice as many papers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week and pays $210 per week for newspapers, how many newspapers does it buy on Monday?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 30
  C: 45
  D: 60
  E: 75
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the hotel buys x newspapers on Monday.
  It buys twice as many newspapers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week, so it buys 2x newspapers on Sunday.
  It buys 1 newspaper for each of the other 6 days of the week, so it buys 6 newspapers in total for the other 6 days of the week.
  The hotel pays $4 for each Sunday newspaper, so it spends 4(2x) = 8x dollars on Sunday newspapers.
  The hotel pays $1 for each of the other 6 newspapers, so it spends 6(x) = 6x dollars on the other 6 newspapers.
  The total cost of the newspapers is $210, so 8x + 6x + 4 = 210.
  Solving for x, we get x = 15.
  Therefore, the hotel buys 15 newspapers on Monday.
  The answer is A: 15.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's call the number of newspapers the hotel buys on Sunday "s" and the number of newspapers it buys on the rest of the days of the week "r".
  From the problem, we know that s = 2r (the hotel orders twice as many papers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week).
  We also know that the hotel pays $4 for each Sunday paper and $1 for each paper on the rest of the days of the week.
  So the total cost per week is 4s + 1(7r) = 4(2r) + 7r = 15r.
  We're told that the hotel pays $210 per week for newspapers, so we can set up the equation 15r = 210 and solve for r.
  15r = 210
  r = 14
  So the hotel buys 14 papers on each of Monday through Saturday.
  We also know that s = 2r, so s = 2(14) = 28.
  Therefore, the hotel buys 14 papers on Monday.
  The answer is A: 15.

Question: Allen starts from X, goes to Y. At the same time Bob starts from Y and goes towards X. Once Allen reaches Y he changes his direction and returns to X. Once Bob reaches X, he changes his direction and returns to Y. Throughout Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob travels at 78kmph. By the time they meet for the second time, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen. Find the distance between X and Y.
Choices:
  A: 144km
  B: 72 km
  C: 126km
  D: 84 km
  E: 48km
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the distance between X and Y is d km.
  Let's assume the time taken by Allen to reach Y from X is t1.
  Let's assume the time taken by Bob to reach X from Y is t2.
  We know that distance = speed x time.
  Therefore, distance covered by Allen in t1 hours = 54t1 km.
  Distance covered by Bob in t2 hours = 78t2 km.
  Distance covered by Allen from Y to X in t1 hours = 54t1 km.
  Distance covered by Bob from X to Y in t2 hours = 78t2 km.
  Total distance covered by Allen = 2 * 54t1 km.
  Total distance covered by Bob = 2 * 78t2 km.
  We know that Bob covers 48 km more than Allen by the time they meet for the second time.
  Therefore, 2 * 78t2 - 2 * 54t1 = 48.
  We also know that the total distance between X and Y is d km.
  Therefore, 2 * 54t1 + 2 * 78t2 = d.
  We have two equations and two variables. We can solve for t1 and t2 and then find d.
  Solving the equations, we get t1 = 2t2/3 and d = 252t2/13.
  Therefore, the distance between X and Y is 252t2/13 km when t2 is the time taken by Bob to reach X from Y.
  We don't know the value of t2 yet, so we can't find the exact distance between X and Y.
  However, we can check which option is closest to 252t2/13 km for some value of t2.
  Let's try t2 = 6 hours (assuming they meet for the second time after 6 hours).
  Then, t1 = 4 hours.
  Distance covered by Allen in 4 hours = 54 * 4 = 216 km.
  Distance covered by Bob in 6 hours = 78 * 6 = 468 km.
  Distance covered by Allen from Y to X in 4 hours = 54 * 4 = 216 km.
  Distance covered by Bob from X to Y in 6 hours = 78 * 6 = 468 km.
  Total distance covered by Allen = 2 * 216 km = 432 km.
  Total distance covered by Bob = 2 * 468 km = 936 km.
  We know that Bob covers 48 km more than Allen by the time they meet for the second time.
  Therefore, 936 - 432 = 504 = 48t2.
  Solving for t2, we get t2 = 10.5 hours.
  Therefore, the distance between X and Y is 252t2/13 = 252 * 10.5 / 13 = 204 km (approx).
  The closest option to 204 km is option D: 84 km.

Thought:
  Let the distance between X and Y be d.
  Let the time taken for Allen to reach Y be t.
  Let the time taken for Bob to reach X be t1.
  Let the time taken for Allen to return to X be t2.
  The distance covered by Allen in t hours = 54t.
  The distance covered by Bob in t1 hours = 78t1.
  When they meet for the first time, the total distance covered = d.
  When they meet for the second time, the total distance covered = 3d.
  The distance covered by Bob when they meet for the second time = 54t2 + 78(t2 - t1) + 48 (since Bob covers 48 km more than Allen).
  We need to find the value of d.
  Therefore, we need to form an equation using the above information and solve for d.
  Let's begin.
  
Calculation:
  Distance covered by Allen in t hours = 54t.
  Distance covered by Bob in t1 hours = 78t1.
  When they meet for the first time, the total distance covered = d.
  Therefore, 54t + 78t1 = d.  --- (Equation 1)
  
  Let's find the value of t1 in terms of t.
  Distance covered by Bob when they meet for the first time = d - 54t.
  Time taken by Bob to cover this distance = (d - 54t)/78.
  Time taken by Bob to reach X = t1.
  Therefore, t1 = t + (d - 54t)/78.  --- (Equation 2)
  
  Let's find the value of t2 in terms of t.
  Distance covered by Allen when they meet for the second time = 2d - 54t.
  Distance covered by Bob when they meet for the second time = 54t2 + 78(t2 - t1) + 48.
  Since they meet at the same time, we can equate the above two distances.
  Therefore, 2d - 54t = 54t2 + 78(t2 - t1) + 48.
  Simplifying the above equation, we get:
  2d - 54t = 54t2 + 78t2 - 78t - 48.
  132t2 - 54t - 2d + 78t + 48 = 0.
  132t2 + 24t - 2d + 48 = 0.  --- (Equation 3)
  
  Let's solve equations 1, 2, and 3 simultaneously to find the value of d.
  From equation 1, we get:
  t = (d - 78t1)/54.
  
  Substituting the value of t in equation 2, we get:
  t1 = (3d + 78t1)/54.
  54t1 = 3d + 78t1.
  54t1 - 78t1 = 3d.
  -24t1 = 3d.
  d = -8t1.  --- (Equation 4)
  
  Substituting the value of t in equation 3, we get:
  132((d - 78t1)/54)^2 + 24((d - 78t1)/54) - 2d + 48 = 0.
  Simplifying the above equation, we get:
  22(d - 78t1)^2 + 4(d - 78t1) - d + 2 = 0.
  22d^2 - 3432t1d + 12312t1^2 + 4d - 312t1 - d + 2 = 0.
  22d^2 - (3432t1 + 1)d + 12312t1^2 - 312t1 + 2 = 0.  --- (Equation 5)
  
  Let's solve equations 4 and 5 simultaneously to find the value of d.
  Substituting the value of d in equation 5, we get a quadratic equation in t1.
  Solving the quadratic equation, we get:
  t1 = 0.1667 or 1.5.
  
  Substituting the value of t1 in equation 4, we get:
  d = -8t1.
  Therefore, d = 1.333 km or 12 km.
  
  Since the distance cannot be in decimals, the answer is 12 km.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 81 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A jeep travels a certain distance taking 6 hours in the forward journey. During the return journey, it increased its speed by 12km/hr and took 4 hours. What is the distance travelled by the jeep?
Choices:
  A: 126km
  B: 144km
  C: 127km
  D: 228km
  E: 128km
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the distance travelled by the jeep is "d" km.
  Let's assume the speed of the jeep in the forward journey is "s" km/hr.
  Let's use the formula: distance = speed x time.
  According to the problem, the jeep travelled "d" km in 6 hours during the forward journey, so we can write:
  d = s x 6
  Rearranging the formula, we get:
  s = d/6
  During the return journey, the speed of the jeep increased by 12km/hr, so the speed became (s+12) km/hr.
  According to the problem, the jeep travelled "d" km in 4 hours during the return journey, so we can write:
  d = (s+12) x 4
  Substituting the value of s from the first equation, we get:
  d = (d/6 + 12) x 4
  Solving for d, we get:
  d = 144 km
  Therefore, the distance travelled by the jeep is 144 km.
  The answer is B: 144km.
Action: Answer("B")

Thought:
  Let's assume the distance travelled by the jeep is "d" km.

  In the forward journey, the jeep took 6 hours to travel the distance "d", so we can write the equation as d = 6s.
  In the return journey, the jeep took 4 hours to travel the same distance "d" at a speed of "s+12" km/hr, so we can write the equation as d = 4(s+12).
  We can solve these equations to find the value of "d".
  d = 6s = 4(s+12)
  6s = 4s + 48
  2s = 48
  s = 24
  d = 6s = 6 x 24 = 144 km.
  Therefore, the distance travelled by the jeep is 144 km.

  2s = 48
  s = 24
  Substituting s=24 into Equation 1, we get:
  d = 24 x 6 = 144
  Therefore, the distance travelled by the jeep is 144km.

Question: The number of water lilies on a certain lake doubles every two days. If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies. In how many days will the lake be fully covered with lilies, if initially there were 64 water lilies on it?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 28
  C: 30
  D: 53
  E: 59
Response 0:
Thought:
  The number of water lilies doubles every two days.
  If there is one water lily, it takes 60 days to fully cover the lake.
  If there are 64 water lilies, the lake is already partially covered.
  We need to find out how many days it will take for the number of water lilies to double enough times to fully cover the lake.
  We can use the formula N = N0 * 2^(t/k), where N is the final number of water lilies, N0 is the initial number of water lilies, t is the time elapsed, and k is the doubling time.
  We can solve for t by plugging in the given values.
  
Calculation:
  N = N0 * 2^(t/k)
  2^6 = 64 * 2^(t/2)
  2^(t/2) = 2^6 / 64
  2^(t/2) = 2^(-2)
  t/2 = -2
  t = -4

  The negative result indicates that the lake was already fully covered 4 days ago. 
  Therefore, the answer is E: 59. 

Action: Answer("E")

  Therefore, 2^(60/2) = 2^30 = the number of lilies on the lake after 60 days if there was initially one lily.
  If there were initially 64 lilies, then the number of lilies on the lake after n days is given by 64*2^(n/2).
  We want to find the number of days it takes for the lake to be fully covered with lilies, so we need to solve the equation 64*2^(n/2) = 2^30.
  Dividing both sides by 64, we get 2^(n/2) = 2^26.
  Taking the logarithm base 2 of both sides, we get n/2 = 26.
  Solving for n, we get n = 52.
  Therefore, it takes 52 days for the lake to be fully covered with lilies if there were initially 64 lilies.

Question: A train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am. Another train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 1030am. At what time do the 2 trains cross one another?
Choices:
  A: 1 hr 23 min
  B: 1 hr 15 min
  C: 1 hr 8 min
  D: 56 min
  E: 55 min
Response 0:
Thought:
  Train M travels for 4 hours from City A to City B.
  Train N travels for 3.5 hours from City B to City A.
  The total distance between City A and City B is the same for both trains.
  Let's assume the two trains meet at X hours after 5 am when Train M and Train N meet.
  Therefore, Train M travels for X hours and Train N travels for (X-2) hours.
  The distance traveled by Train M is (X/4) and the distance traveled by Train N is (X-2)/3.5.
  Since the total distance traveled by both trains is the same, we can equate the two distances.
  (X/4) = (X-2)/3.5
  Solving for X, we get X = 14/3 hours after 5 am.
  Converting 14/3 hours to hours and minutes, we get 4 hours and 40 minutes.
  Therefore, the two trains cross each other at 9:40 am.
  The answer is not one of the choices given.

  x = (2 * Speed of Train N)/(Speed of Train M + Speed of Train N)
  Once we find the value of x, we can add it to the time taken by Train N to find the total time.
  The answer will be in hours and minutes.

  We can use the formula: speed = distance/time to solve for the speed of the trains.
  Let's assume the speed of Train M is s1 and the speed of Train N is s2.
  We can write two equations based on the above information:
  (d/2) = s1*(4+x)  (distance = speed * time)
  (d/2) = s2*(3.5-x)
  We can solve for x by equating the two equations:
  s1*(4+x) = s2*(3.5-x)
  4s1 + xs1 = 3.5s2 - xs2
  xs1 + xs2 = 3.5s2 - 4s1
  x = (3.5s2 - 4s1)/(s1 + s2)
  We can now substitute the values of s1 and s2:
  s1 = (d/2)/4 = d/8
  s2 = (d/2)/3.5 = d/7
  x = (3.5*(d/7) - 4*(d/8))/((d/8) + (d/7))

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 84 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The average (arithmetic mean) of the weight of 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons. The average weight of the group of vehicles increased by 2.6 tons after a new heavy duty truck was added to the group? What is the weight in tons of the heavy duty truck?
Choices:
  A: 40.8
  B: 41.6
  C: 42.2
  D: 43.5
  E: 44.8
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the weight of the new heavy-duty truck is x tons.
  The sum of the weights of the 10 vehicles before the new truck was added is 10*12.2 = 122 tons.
  The sum of the weights of the 11 vehicles after the new truck was added is 11*(12.2+2.6) = 157.2 tons.
  Therefore, the weight of the new heavy-duty truck is x = 157.2 - 122 = 35.2 tons.
  The answer is A: 40.8.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's call the weight of the new heavy duty truck "x".
  The sum of the weights of the original 10 vehicles is 10 * 12.2 = 122.
  After the new truck is added, there are 11 vehicles in the group.
  The new average weight is 12.2 + 2.6 = 14.8.
  The sum of the weights of all 11 vehicles is 11 * 14.8 = 162.8.
  The sum of the weights of the original 10 vehicles plus the weight of the new truck is 122 + x.
  We can set up an equation: (122 + x) / 11 = 14.8
  Solving for x, we get x = 41.6.
  Therefore, the weight of the heavy duty truck is 41.6 tons.

  So, we can write the equation: (10 * 12.2 + x) / 11 = 14.8
  Solving for x, we get x = 41.6
  Therefore, the weight of the heavy duty truck is 41.6 tons.

Choices:

  B: 20/7
  C: 30/7
  D: 40/7
  E: 50/7

- We want to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand.

- Let's say we remove x kg of the mixture.
- The amount of sand in the remaining mixture is 0.3 * (10 - x) kg.
- We want to add some pure sand to make the total amount of sand equal to the total amount of clay.
- The amount of clay in the remaining mixture is 0.7 * (10 - x) kg.
- This means we need to add (0.7 * (10 - x) - 0.3 * (10 - x)) kg of pure sand.
- Simplifying this expression, we get 0.4 * (10 - x) kg of pure sand.
- We want the final mixture to be 50% sand, which means the amount of pure sand we add should be equal to the amount of mixture we remove.
- This means 0.4 * (10 - x) = x.
- Solving for x, we get x = 4 kg.
- Therefore, we need to remove 4 kg of the mixture and replace it with 1.6 kg of pure sand.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 88 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: What will be the cost of gardening 1-metre – broad boundary around a rectangular plot having perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre?
Choices:
  A: 3400
  B: 1700
  C: 3440
  D: Cannot be determined
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the length and breadth of the rectangular plot are L and B respectively.
  Perimeter of the rectangular plot = 2(L+B) = 340
  L + B = 170
  The breadth of the rectangular plot with a 1-meter boundary will be B + 2 and the length will be L + 2.
  The area of the rectangular plot with a 1-meter boundary = (L+2) * (B+2)
  The area of the rectangular plot = L * B
  The area of the boundary = Area of the plot with a 1-meter boundary - Area of the plot
  Area of the boundary = (L+2) * (B+2) - L * B
  Area of the boundary = L + 2B + 4
  The cost of gardening 1 square meter of the boundary = 10
  The cost of gardening the entire boundary = Area of the boundary * 10
  The cost of gardening the entire boundary = (L + 2B + 4) * 10
  The value of L + 2B = 170 + 4 = 174
  The cost of gardening the entire boundary = 174 * 10
  The cost of gardening the entire boundary = 1740
  Therefore, the answer is A: 3400.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the length of the rectangular plot is L and the width is W.
  The perimeter of the rectangular plot is given as 340 meters.
  The perimeter of a rectangle is given by the formula 2(L+W).
  So, 2(L+W) = 340, which simplifies to L+W = 170.
  The length of the boundary around the rectangular plot will be L+2 and the width will be W+2.
  The area of the boundary will be (L+2)(W+2) - LW.
  The cost of gardening 1 square meter of the boundary is 10.
  Therefore, the cost of gardening the entire boundary will be 10 times the area of the boundary.
  After simplification, the expression for the cost of gardening the boundary will be 20L + 20W + 36.
  We know that L+W = 170, so we can substitute this value in the expression for the cost of gardening the boundary.
  After substitution, the expression becomes 20(170) + 36 = 3440.
  Therefore, the cost of gardening the boundary will be 3440.

Question: Calculate the percentage gain of a merchant who purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450 and sold the whole lot at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg.
Choices:
  A: 50 %
  B: 60 %
  C: 55 %
  D: 70 %
  E: 58%
Response 0:
Thought:
  The cost price of 1 kg of oranges is Rs. 450/90 = Rs. 5.
  The selling price of 1 kg of oranges is Rs. 7.50.
  Profit per kg of oranges = Selling price - Cost price = Rs. 7.50 - Rs. 5 = Rs. 2.50.
  Profit percentage = (Profit / Cost price) * 100.
  Profit percentage = (2.50 / 5) * 100 = 50%.
  Therefore, the percentage gain of the merchant is 50%.

  B: 48
  C: 50
  D: 55
  E: 58

  From the second statement, we know that when J = F, S + (F - S) * 2 = 2S.
  Simplifying this equation, we get F - S = S, which means F = 2S.
  From the third statement, we know that when J = F, F = 2(S - F + J).
  Simplifying this equation using F = 2S, we get J = 3F/2 - S/2.
  Substituting J and F in the first equation, we get 3F/2 + S = 100.
  Substituting F = 2S in the above equation, we get 5S = 200, which means S = 40.
  Substituting S in F = 2S, we get F = 80.
  Therefore, the age of Joe's father is 80.

Topic: Math
Question: Christopher and Jonathan were having bets. They decide that a coin will be flipped twenty times and each time it turns heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan and each time it turns out to be Tails, Jonathan will give 3$ to Christopher. After flipping for twenty times none of the both won or lost any amount.
How many times did the coin landed on Heads ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 23
  C: 16
  D: 18
  E: 12
Response 0:
Thought:
  Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan for each Heads.
  Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher for each Tails.
  Let's assume that the coin landed on Heads x times.
  Therefore, the coin landed on Tails (20-x) times.
  Christopher gave $2x to Jonathan.
  Jonathan gave $3(20-x) to Christopher.
  Since none of them won or lost any amount, the total amount given by Christopher is equal to the total amount given by Jonathan.
  2x = 60 - 3x
  5x = 60
  x = 12
  Therefore, the coin landed on Heads 12 times.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Christopher pays $2 for each Head and receives $3 for each Tail.
  The difference between the amount paid for each Head and the amount received for each Tail is $1.
  The total difference between the amount paid and the amount received is zero.
  Therefore, the number of Heads must be equal to the number of Tails.
  The total number of flips is 20.
  Therefore, the number of Heads is 10.

  5x = 60

Topic: Math
Question: Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. What is the distance between A and B?
Choices:
  A: 180
  B: 90
  C: 270
  D: 360
  E: None of the above
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let d be the distance between A and B.
  Let t1 be the time it takes Kevin to drive from A to B.
  Let t2 be the time it takes Kevin to drive from B to A.
  We know that d = 70t1 and d = 90t2.
  We also know that 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it.
  This means that he has already driven 70 miles from B, and has 70 miles left to drive to A.
  We can set up the equation: 70 = 90(t2 - 3).
  Solving for t2, we get t2 = 23/3.
  Substituting into d = 90t2, we get d = 690.
  Therefore, the distance between A and B is 690 miles.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's call the distance between A and B "d".
  We know that Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph.
  Therefore, the time it took him to travel from A to B is given by the formula: time = distance / speed = d / 70.
  We also know that once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph.
  Therefore, the time it took him to travel from B to A is given by the formula: time = distance / speed = d / 90.
  We know that exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it.
  Therefore, the time it took him to travel from the point where he was 70 miles away from B to B is 70 / 70 = 1 hour.
  We also know that this happened 3 hours before the end of his trip, which means that the total time of his trip is 4 hours.
  Therefore, the time it took him to travel from A to the point where he was 70 miles away from B is 4 - 1 - (d / 90) = 3 - (d / 90).
  We can now set up an equation using the formula: time = distance / speed.
  We know that the time it took him to travel from A to B is d / 70, and the time it took him to travel from A to the point where he was 70 miles away from B is 3 - (d / 90).
  Therefore, we have the equation: d / 70 + 3 - (d / 90) = 4.
  Solving for d, we get: d = 270.
  Therefore, the distance between A and B is 270 miles.
  The answer is C: 270.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 97 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 200
  C: 400
  D: 100
  E: 500
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that there are 'n' employees in the organization.
  Each employee contributes 'x' amount of money.
  Therefore, the total amount collected would be n*x.
  As per the problem, n*x = 6,00,000 and (n*x + 60n) = 6,24,000.
  Solving the above equations, we can get the value of 'n'.
  n = 200
  Therefore, there are 200 employees in that organization.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's assume that there are 'n' employees in the organization.
  The organization wants to raise Rs. 6 lakh, so each employee would contribute Rs. 6 lakh / n.
  If each employee had contributed Rs. 60 extra, then each employee would contribute Rs. (6.24 lakh / n).
  According to the problem, the difference between the two contributions is Rs. 60.
  Therefore, we can form the following equation: (6.24 lakh / n) - (6 lakh / n) = 60.
  Solving this equation for 'n' will give us the number of employees in the organization.
  Simplifying the equation, we get: (0.24 lakh / n) = 60.
  Multiplying both sides by 'n', we get: 0.24 lakh = 60n.
  Dividing both sides by 60, we get: n = 400.
  Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.
Action: Answer("C")

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 98 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A man divides Rs 8600 among 5 sons, 4 daughters and 2 nephews. If each daughter receives four times as much as each nephew, and each son receives five as much as each nephew. How much does each daughter receive ?
Choices:
  A: Rs 400
  B: Rs 500
  C: Rs 600
  D: Rs 700
  E: Rs 800
Response 0:
Thought:
Let the amount each nephew receives be x.
Each daughter receives 4 times as much as each nephew, so each daughter receives 4x.
Each son receives 5 times as much as each nephew, so each son receives 5x.
There are 5 sons, 4 daughters, and 2 nephews, so there are 11 total people receiving money.
The total amount of money is Rs 8600.
We can set up an equation to solve for x:
2x + 4(4x) + 5(5x) = 8600
Simplifying the equation:
2x + 16x + 25x = 8600
43x = 8600
x = 200
Each daughter receives 4 times as much as each nephew, so each daughter receives 4x = 4(200) = Rs 800.
Therefore, the answer is E: Rs 800.

Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let the share of each nephew be x.
Then, the share of each daughter is 4x and the share of each son is 5x.
The total number of people who receive the money is 5+4+2 = 11.
Therefore, we can write the equation: 5(5x) + 4(4x) + 2(x) = 8600
Simplifying the equation, we get: 39x = 8600
So, x = 220
Therefore, each daughter receives 4x = 4*220 = 880
The answer is Rs 880.

### Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 99 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A student instead of finding the value of 7/8 of a number, found the value of 7/18 of the number. If his answer differed from the actual one by 770, find the that number.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 2520
  C: 1728
  D: 1656
  E: None
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let the actual number be x.
  The student found the value of 7/18 of the number which is (7/18)x.
  The actual value of 7/8 of the number is (7/8)x.
  The difference between the student's answer and the actual answer is 770.
  Therefore, (7/8)x - (7/18)x = 770.
  Simplifying, we get (35/72)x = 770.
  Solving for x, we get x = (770*72)/35 = 1584.
  Therefore, the number is 1584.
  The answer is A: 1584.

Question: Calculate the maximum distance you can travel with $8.50 on a cab which charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
Choices:
  A: 11.75 miles
  B: 12.75 miles
  C: 17.75 miles
  D: 14.75 miles
  E: 10.75 miles
Response 0:
Thought:
  The cab charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
  Let's assume that the maximum distance we can travel is x miles.
  The first quarter-mile costs $3.50, which means we have $5.00 left to spend on the remaining distance.
  The remaining distance is (x - 0.25) miles.
  For each additional quarter mile, the cab charges 10 cents, which is equivalent to $0.10.
  Therefore, the cost of the remaining distance is 0.10 * (4 * (x - 0.25)) = 0.40 * (x - 0.25).
  The total cost of the trip should be less than or equal to $8.50.
  Therefore, we can write the following inequality: 3.50 + 0.40 * (x - 0.25) <= 8.50.
  Solving the inequality, we get x <= 12.75.
  Therefore, the maximum distance we can travel is 12.75 miles.
